ASSISTANT:
I've reviewed both documents and written the final plan. Here's my assessment:

## Verdict on your plan: solid — no architectural problems

Your `code-review-platform-plan.md` correctly covers all 9 hard requirements: async POST/GET separation, reject-on-full (503, no queueing), cache reuse **with in-flight dedup**, 24h TTL with both a cleanup task and a lazy 404 guard, rules-as-data, and fully parametrized Ollama config. The trickiest correctness details — acquiring the slot synchronously in the POST handler (not `await`-ing the semaphore), releasing in `finally`, and putting the cache check *before* the capacity check — were all right.

## Corrections I folded in

1. **Python version** — your default `python3` is 3.8 (EOL, won't run SQLAlchemy 2.0 async cleanly). I'll use the installed `python3.12` and add a `.python-version` file.
2. **Dev deps split** (your global rule) — pytest/pytest-asyncio go in `requirements-dev.txt`, runtime deps in `requirements.txt`.
3. **CapacityLimiter** — a plain integer counter is cleaner and provably race-free in a single-threaded loop, vs. the semaphore + `.locked()` workaround your plan flagged as awkward.
4. **LLM output** — using Ollama's native `format` (JSON schema) + your defensive parser, per your choice.
5. **SQLite concurrency** — added `PRAGMA journal_mode=WAL` + `busy_timeout` (your plan only had `foreign_keys=ON`); with 5 parallel writers you'd otherwise risk "database is locked".
6. **Slot-leak window** — release the slot if row-insert/`create_task` throws *before* the background task starts.
7. **API** — multipart-only, per your choice.

Good news: `qwen2.5-coder:7b` is already pulled, so manual E2E testing is ready to go.

One note: this directory isn't a git repo yet, so `git init` will be the first step toward the GitHub deliverable.

a service that accepts a Python source file, runs LLM-based rule checks locally via Ollama,

(`code-review-platform-plan.md`). This plan **follows that design** — it is sound and covers
all 9 hard requirements — with a small set of corrections and refinements found during review,
plus alignment to the user's global coding rules (`~/.claude/CLAUDE.md`).

Environment confirmed: greenfield directory; Ollama installed with `qwen2.5-coder:7b` already
pulled; `python3.12` available (system `python3` is 3.8 — too old, **do not use it**).

Now let's smoke-test the DB layer end-to-end against a temp SQLite file (not the project's `.db`).

  [TOOL CALL: Bash]
  $ cd "/Users/idansahar/Desktop/Code Reviewer" && source .venv/bin/activate && rm -f /tmp/code_review_smoketest.db* && DATABASE_URL="sqlite+aiosqlite:////tmp/code_review_smoketest.db" python - <<'EOF'
import asyncio

from app.db.session import engine, init_db, async_session_factory
from app.db import repository as repo
from app.db.models import ScanStatus


async def main():
    await init_db()
    async with async_session_factory() as session:
        scan = await repo.create_scan(session, content_hash="abc123", filename="test.py", code="print('hi')")
        assert scan.status == ScanStatus.PENDING.value
        scan_id = scan.id

        reused = await repo.find_reusable_scan(session, "abc123")
        assert reused is not None and reused.id == scan_id

        await repo.mark_running(session, scan_id)
        await repo.save_rule_result(session, scan_id, "rule1", "Meaningful variable names", True, "looks fine")
        await repo.save_rule_result(session, scan_id, "rule2", "Docstring matches logic", False, "docstring is stale")
        await repo.mark_completed(session, scan_id)

        fetched = await repo.get_scan(session, scan_id)
        assert fetched is not None
        assert fetched.status == ScanStatus.COMPLETED.value
        assert len(fetched.results) == 2
        assert {r.rule_id for r in fetched.results} == {"rule1", "rule2"}

        # TTL=0 -> the just-created scan is treated as expired
        assert await repo.get_scan(session, scan_id, ttl_hours=0) is None
        assert await repo.find_reusable_scan(session, "abc123", ttl_hours=0) is None

        deleted = await repo.delete_expired_scans(session, ttl_hours=0)
        assert deleted == 1
        assert await repo.get_scan(session, scan_id) is None

    await engine.dispose()
    print("DB SMOKE TEST OK")


asyncio.run(main())
EOF

import asyncio

from app.db.session import engine, init_db, async_session_factory
from app.db import repository as repo
from app.db.models import ScanStatus


async def main():
    await init_db()
    async with async_session_factory() as session:
        scan = await repo.create_scan(session, content_hash="abc123", filename="test.py", code="print('hi')")
        assert scan.status == ScanStatus.PENDING.value
        scan_id = scan.id

        reused = await repo.find_reusable_scan(session, "abc123")
        assert reused is not None and reused.id == scan_id

        await repo.save_rule_result(session, scan_id, "rule1", "Meaningful variable names", True, "looks fine")

        await repo.mark_completed(session, scan_id)

        fetched = await repo.get_scan(session, scan_id)
        assert fetched is not None
        assert fetched.status == ScanStatus.COMPLETED.value
        assert len(fetched.results) == 2
        assert {r.rule_id for r in fetched.results} == {"rule1", "rule2"}

        # TTL=0 -> the just-created scan is treated as expired

        assert await repo.find_reusable_scan(session, "abc123", ttl_hours=0) is None

        assert deleted == 1

ASSISTANT:
## Step 2 complete — review please

**Created:**
- `app/db/models.py` — SQLAlchemy 2.0 declarative models:
  - `Scan`: `id` (uuid4), `content_hash`, `filename`, `code`, `status`, `created_at`/`completed_at` (naive UTC datetimes — avoids SQLite tz round-trip issues, per the plan's pitfall note), `error`. Indexes on `(content_hash, status, created_at)` for cache lookup and `(created_at)` for TTL cleanup, plus a **partial unique index** on `content_hash` for `pending`/`running` rows (defensive backstop for the in-flight dedup, to be paired with an `asyncio.Lock` in step 6).
  - `RuleResult`: `scan_id` FK with `ON DELETE CASCADE`, `rule_id`, `rule_name`, `adheres` (nullable bool), `detail`.
  - `ScanStatus` enum: pending/running/completed/failed.
- `app/db/session.py` — async engine from `settings.database_url`, sets `PRAGMA journal_mode=WAL`, `busy_timeout=5000`, `foreign_keys=ON` on every connection; `init_db()` creates tables; `get_session()` dependency for FastAPI.
- `app/db/repository.py` — `find_reusable_scan` (non-expired, status in pending/running/completed, newest first), `create_scan`, `mark_running`, `save_rule_result`, `mark_completed`, `mark_failed`, `get_scan` (with eager-loaded results, expiry-aware), `delete_expired_scans`. All TTL-aware functions take an optional `ttl_hours` override (defaults to `settings.result_ttl_hours`) for testability.

**Verified:** ran a full smoke test against a temp SQLite DB (deleted afterward) — create → reuse lookup → mark running → save 2 rule results → mark completed → fetch with eager-loaded results → TTL=0 makes both `get_scan` and `find_reusable_scan` treat the row as expired → `delete_expired_scans` removes it and cascades the rule results. All assertions passed.

**Not yet done (next step):** Rules YAML + LLM client (Ollama with `format` JSON schema) + defensive verdict parser.

take a look at this file, i think it is better for the llm client:
from __future__ import annotations

import ollama


class OllamaClient:
    """Thin wrapper around ollama.Client; base_url and model are injected
    so config.py controls which provider/model is used."""

    def __init__(self, base_url: str, model: str, timeout: float = 120.0) -> None:
        self._model = model
        self._client = ollama.Client(host=base_url, timeout=timeout)

    def generate(self, prompt: str) -> str:
        response = self._client.generate(
            model=self._model,
            prompt=prompt,
            format="json",   # instructs Ollama to constrain output to valid JSON
            stream=False,
            options={"temperature": 0},  # keep it deterministic
        )
        return response.response

ASSISTANT:
This is a good simplification — the official `ollama` package handles connection/serialization for us. A few things I'll adjust to fit our setup:

- Use `ollama.AsyncClient` (not the sync `Client`) — our scanner runs inside FastAPI's async event loop, and a sync HTTP call would block other concurrent scans, defeating the 5-parallel-scan requirement.
- Keep `format` as our **JSON schema** (not the string `"json"`) — we already validated schema-constrained output gives us exactly `{"adheres":..., "reason":...}` reliably, which is the "Native JSON + parsing" approach you picked earlier. Generic `format="json"` only guarantees *valid JSON*, not that shape.
- `options={"temperature": 0}` is a nice addition — more deterministic verdicts, which also helps cache-hit consistency. I'll keep it.
- Keep the existing `LLMClient` Protocol (`complete()`) so the rest of the code (and step 4) doesn't change — just rewrite `OllamaClient`'s internals.

import asyncio

from app.db.session import engine, init_db, async_session_factory
from app.db import repository as repo
from app.db.models import ScanStatus
from app.reviewer.scanner import run_scan
from app.reviewer.rules import RULES


class FakeLLMClient:
    """Returns canned responses in order; raises on call N if configured."""

    def __init__(self, responses, raise_on_call=None):
        self.responses = list(responses)
        self.raise_on_call = raise_on_call
        self.call_count = 0

    async def complete(self, prompt, *, json_schema=None):
        self.call_count += 1
        if self.raise_on_call == self.call_count:
            raise RuntimeError("simulated LLM failure")
        return self.responses.pop(0)


async def main():
    await init_db()

    # --- Case 1: both rules succeed -> scan completed ---
    async with async_session_factory() as session:
        scan = await repo.create_scan(session, content_hash="h1", filename="a.py", code="x=1")
        scan_id = scan.id

    released = {"called": False}
    client = FakeLLMClient([
        '{"adheres": true, "reason": "fine"}',
        '{"adheres": false, "reason": "bad docstring"}',
    ])
    await run_scan(scan_id, "x=1", llm_client=client, release_slot=lambda: released.__setitem__("called", True))

    async with async_session_factory() as session:
        fetched = await repo.get_scan(session, scan_id)
        assert fetched.status == ScanStatus.COMPLETED.value, fetched.status
        results = {r.rule_id: r.adheres for r in fetched.results}
        assert results == {RULES[0].id: True, RULES[1].id: False}, results
    assert released["called"] is True
    print("CASE 1 OK: completed scan with correct verdicts, slot released")

    # --- Case 2: second rule's response is unparseable -> scan failed, partial results kept ---
    async with async_session_factory() as session:
        scan = await repo.create_scan(session, content_hash="h2", filename="b.py", code="y=2")
        scan_id2 = scan.id

    released2 = {"called": False}
    client2 = FakeLLMClient([
        '{"adheres": true, "reason": "fine"}',
        'complete nonsense, no boolean here',
    ])
    await run_scan(scan_id2, "y=2", llm_client=client2, release_slot=lambda: released2.__setitem__("called", True))

    async with async_session_factory() as session:
        fetched2 = await repo.get_scan(session, scan_id2)
        assert fetched2.status == ScanStatus.FAILED.value, fetched2.status
        assert fetched2.error and "Could not parse verdict" in fetched2.error, fetched2.error
        assert len(fetched2.results) == 1, fetched2.results
    assert released2["called"] is True
    print("CASE 2 OK: parse failure -> scan failed, partial results retained, slot released")

    # --- Case 3: first LLM call raises -> scan failed, no results ---
    async with async_session_factory() as session:
        scan = await repo.create_scan(session, content_hash="h3", filename="c.py", code="z=3")
        scan_id3 = scan.id

    released3 = {"called": False}
    client3 = FakeLLMClient(['unused'], raise_on_call=1)
    await run_scan(scan_id3, "z=3", llm_client=client3, release_slot=lambda: released3.__setitem__("called", True))

    async with async_session_factory() as session:
        fetched3 = await repo.get_scan(session, scan_id3)
        assert fetched3.status == ScanStatus.FAILED.value, fetched3.status
        assert "simulated LLM failure" in fetched3.error, fetched3.error
        assert len(fetched3.results) == 0
    assert released3["called"] is True
    print("CASE 3 OK: LLM exception -> scan failed, no results, slot released")

    await engine.dispose()
    print("SCANNER SMOKE TEST OK")


asyncio.run(main())

ASSISTANT:
## Step 4 complete — review please

**Created:** `app/reviewer/scanner.py` — `run_scan(scan_id, code, *, llm_client, release_slot)`:
- Marks the scan `running`.
- Iterates `RULES` sequentially, calling the LLM with `VERDICT_SCHEMA`, parsing the verdict, and persisting each `rule_results` row as it goes (each DB op uses its own short-lived session via a small `_run` helper, per the "short-lived sessions" guidance).
- On success, marks the scan `completed`.
- **Design decision**: any exception (LLM error, timeout, or unparseable verdict) marks the **whole scan** `failed` with the error message stored on `scans.error`, rather than a per-rule "errored" status. I went this way because `rule_results.adheres` is `bool|None` with no per-row status field, and the `GET /scans/{id}` contract only specifies `adheres: true|false` — a whole-scan failure is simpler and fits the existing schema/contract without adding a new column. Partial results from rules that succeeded before the failure are kept in the DB (informational).
- `release_slot: Callable[[], None]` is a required callback, called in `finally` — keeps the scanner decoupled from `CapacityLimiter` (step 5), which will supply the real callback when wiring routes in step 6.
- `llm_client: LLMClient` is required (no default) — explicit DI, easy to mock in tests, real `OllamaClient` wired in step 6.

**Verified** (temp SQLite DB, cleaned up after): 3 cases — both rules succeed → `completed` with correct TRUE/FALSE verdicts; rule 2 returns unparseable text → `failed` with error message, rule 1's result still persisted; LLM raises mid-call → `failed`, no results. In all three, `release_slot()` fired exactly once.

  content: from __future__ import annotations


class CapacityLimiter:
    """Non-blocking concurrency cap.

    try_acquire() either reserves a slot and returns True, or returns False
    immediately if at capacity. Callers must reject the request on False, not
    wait for a slot to free up. Safe in a single-threaded asyncio event loop:
    there is no `await` between the capacity check and the increment.

... [truncated, 1030 chars total]

  [TOOL RESULT]
File created successfully at: /Users/idansahar/Desktop/Code Reviewer/app/core/capacity.py (file state is current in your context — no need to Read it back)

  [TOOL CALL: Bash]
  $ cd "/Users/idansahar/Desktop/Code Reviewer" && source .venv/bin/activate && python - <<'EOF'
from app.core.capacity import CapacityLimiter

limiter = CapacityLimiter(max_concurrent=5)

# fill to capacity
for _ in range(5):
    assert limiter.try_acquire() is True
assert limiter.in_use == 5

# 6th request rejected, no state change
assert limiter.try_acquire() is False
assert limiter.in_use == 5

# release frees a slot
limiter.release()
assert limiter.in_use == 4
assert limiter.try_acquire() is True
assert limiter.in_use == 5

# double-release is a programming error -> raises
for _ in range(5):
    limiter.release()
try:
    limiter.release()
    raise SystemExit("expected RuntimeError on over-release")
except RuntimeError:
    pass

print("CAPACITY LIMITER OK")
EOF   # Verify CapacityLimiter behavior

ASSISTANT:
## Step 5 complete — review please

**Created:** `app/core/capacity.py` — `CapacityLimiter(max_concurrent)`:
- `try_acquire() -> bool`: returns `False` immediately if at capacity (no waiting), otherwise reserves a slot. No `await` between check and increment, so it's race-free in the single-threaded event loop.
- `release()`: frees a slot; raises `RuntimeError` on over-release (catches double-release bugs early).
- `in_use` property for visibility.
- No dependency on `settings` — the actual instance (sized via `MAX_PARALLEL_SCANS`) gets constructed and wired into routes in step 6, keeping this class independently testable.

**Verified:** fill to 5/5 → 6th `try_acquire()` rejected with no state change → `release()` frees a slot → re-acquire succeeds → over-release raises `RuntimeError`.

**Not yet done (next step):** API routes — `POST /scans` (cache-check under `asyncio.Lock` → capacity-check → insert → spawn task, with slot release on spawn failure), `GET /scans/{id}` with expiry guard, `/health`. This is the step where scanner, capacity limiter, repository, and DB session all get wired together into the FastAPI app.

Ready for Step 6.

================================================================================
USER:
dont we need to use semaphore in the capacity?

ASSISTANT:
No — a plain `asyncio.Semaphore` is actually the wrong tool here, and this was a deliberate change from your original plan (refinement #3). Here's why:

**`Semaphore.acquire()` is designed to wait/queue** when the count is exhausted — that's its whole purpose. But requirement #3 demands *immediate rejection* (503), not queueing. To make a semaphore non-blocking, you'd have to do:

```python
if not sem.locked():
    await sem.acquire()
else:
    return 503
```

This *happens* to be race-free in a single-threaded event loop, but only because of an implementation detail: `Semaphore.acquire()` doesn't actually hit an `await` suspension point when `_value > 0`. That's relying on `asyncio` internals, not documented contract — fragile if the implementation ever changes, and easy to break accidentally (e.g., someone inserts an `await` between the `locked()` check and `acquire()`).

**Our `CapacityLimiter`** (`app/core/capacity.py`) does the same job with zero `await`s anywhere:

```python
def try_acquire(self) -> bool:
    if self._in_use >= self._max_concurrent:
        return False
    self._in_use += 1
    return True
```

Since there's no `await` between the check and the increment, there's no possible event-loop context switch — it's provably atomic, simple integer arithmetic. Same guarantee as the semaphore workaround, but explicit and not dependent on internals.

(Note: this is per-process, which is fine since the app runs as a single `uvicorn` process/event loop — multi-worker/multi-process scaling is explicitly out of scope for this POC.)

So no change needed — ready to continue to Step 6 whenever you are.

================================================================================
USER:
so we basicly built our own semaphore?

ASSISTANT:
Yes, essentially — `CapacityLimiter` *is* a counting semaphore conceptually (an integer count of available permits, capped at `max_concurrent`).

The difference is we stripped it down to only the part we need: a non-blocking "try" operation. `asyncio.Semaphore` is built around `await acquire()` — a *blocking* primitive with an internal waiter queue (futures, FIFO wakeups, etc.) for callers willing to wait their turn. We don't want any of that machinery — requirement #3 explicitly forbids waiting/queueing.

So: same core idea (a counter with permits), minus the waiting/queueing half of a semaphore that we'd never use and that would actively work against the "reject immediately" requirement. It's sometimes called a "non-blocking counting gate" — same concept, smaller and purpose-fit.

Ready to continue to Step 6?

ASSISTANT:
Now let's verify the full route wiring with a smoke test against a temp DB — covering validation errors, 404, the cache/in-flight-dedup flow, capacity rejection + release, and `/health`, all with a mocked LLM client (no real Ollama needed for this check).

  [TOOL CALL: Bash]
  $ cd "/Users/idansahar/Desktop/Code Reviewer" && source .venv/bin/activate && rm -f /tmp/routes_smoketest.db /tmp/routes_smoketest.db-wal /tmp/routes_smoketest.db-shm /tmp/routes_smoketest.db-journal && DATABASE_URL="sqlite+aiosqlite:////tmp/routes_smoketest.db" python - <<'EOF'
import asyncio

import httpx

from app.main import app
from app.api import routes
from app.db.session import init_db, engine
from app.core.capacity import CapacityLimiter


class FakeLLMClient:
    def __init__(self, gate: asyncio.Event, responses, reachable=True):
        self.gate = gate
        self.responses = list(responses)
        self.call_count = 0
        self._reachable = reachable

    async def complete(self, prompt, *, json_schema=None):
        await self.gate.wait()
        self.call_count += 1
        return self.responses[(self.call_count - 1) % len(self.responses)]

    async def is_reachable(self):
        return self._reachable


async def main():
    await init_db()

    transport = httpx.ASGITransport(app=app)
    async with httpx.AsyncClient(transport=transport, base_url="http://test") as client:

        # --- A: validation errors ---
        r = await client.post("/scans", files={"file": ("test.txt", b"print(1)", "text/plain")})
        assert r.status_code == 422, r.text
        r = await client.post("/scans", files={"file": ("empty.py", b"", "text/plain")})
        assert r.status_code == 422, r.text
        print("A OK: non-.py and empty file -> 422")

        # --- B: 404 ---
        r = await client.get("/scans/00000000-0000-0000-0000-000000000000")
        assert r.status_code == 404, r.text
        print("B OK: unknown scan -> 404")

        # --- C: submit, in-flight dedup, completion, cache hit ---
        gate_c = asyncio.Event()
        fake_c = FakeLLMClient(gate_c, [
            '{"adheres": true, "reason": "fine"}',
            '{"adheres": false, "reason": "bad docstring"}',
        ])
        app.dependency_overrides[routes.get_llm_client] = lambda: fake_c

        code_a = "x = 1\nprint(x)\n"
        r1 = await client.post("/scans", files={"file": ("a.py", code_a.encode(), "text/plain")})
        assert r1.status_code == 202, r1.text
        body1 = r1.json()
        assert body1["cached"] is False
        scan_id = body1["scan_id"]

        # second submission of identical content while first is still running (gate not set)
        r2 = await client.post("/scans", files={"file": ("a.py", code_a.encode(), "text/plain")})
        assert r2.status_code == 202, r2.text
        body2 = r2.json()
        assert body2["cached"] is True and body2["scan_id"] == scan_id, body2
        print("C1 OK: in-flight dedup returns same scan_id, cached=true")

        gate_c.set()
        for _ in range(200):
            r = await client.get(f"/scans/{scan_id}")
            if r.json()["status"] == "completed":
                break
            await asyncio.sleep(0.02)
        else:
            raise AssertionError("scan never completed")

        result = r.json()
        results_by_rule = {x["rule_id"]: x["adheres"] for x in result["results"]}
        assert results_by_rule == {"meaningful_variable_names": True, "docstring_matches_logic": False}, results_by_rule
        print("C2 OK: scan completed with correct verdicts")

        # resubmission of same content -> cache hit, no new LLM calls
        r3 = await client.post("/scans", files={"file": ("a.py", code_a.encode(), "text/plain")})
        assert r3.status_code == 200, r3.text
        body3 = r3.json()
        assert body3["cached"] is True and body3["scan_id"] == scan_id and body3["status"] == "completed"
        assert fake_c.call_count == 2, fake_c.call_count
        print("C3 OK: completed cache hit, zero additional LLM calls")

        # --- D: capacity limit ---
        gate_d = asyncio.Event()
        fake_d = FakeLLMClient(gate_d, ['{"adheres": true, "reason": "ok"}'])
        app.dependency_overrides[routes.get_llm_client] = lambda: fake_d
        small_limiter = CapacityLimiter(max_concurrent=1)
        app.dependency_overrides[routes.get_capacity_limiter] = lambda: small_limiter

        rb = await client.post("/scans", files={"file": ("b.py", b"b = 2\n", "text/plain")})
        assert rb.status_code == 202, rb.text
        scan_b = rb.json()["scan_id"]

        rc = await client.post("/scans", files={"file": ("c.py", b"c = 3\n", "text/plain")})
        assert rc.status_code == 503, rc.text
        assert "capacity" in rc.json()["detail"].lower()
        print("D1 OK: 6th-equivalent request rejected with 503 while slot is held")

        # release the held slot, then a new submission should succeed again
        gate_d.set()
        for _ in range(200):
            r = await client.get(f"/scans/{scan_b}")
            if r.json()["status"] == "completed":
                break
            await asyncio.sleep(0.02)
        else:
            raise AssertionError("scan b never completed")

        rd = await client.post("/scans", files={"file": ("d.py", b"d = 4\n", "text/plain")})
        assert rd.status_code == 202, rd.text
        print("D2 OK: slot freed after completion, new submission accepted")

        # --- E: health ---
        app.dependency_overrides[routes.get_llm_client] = lambda: FakeLLMClient(asyncio.Event(), [], reachable=True)
        r = await client.get("/health")
        assert r.json() == {"status": "ok", "ollama_reachable": True}, r.json()

        app.dependency_overrides[routes.get_llm_client] = lambda: FakeLLMClient(asyncio.Event(), [], reachable=False)
        r = await client.get("/health")
        assert r.json() == {"status": "ok", "ollama_reachable": False}, r.json()
        print("E OK: /health reflects ollama reachability")

    app.dependency_overrides.clear()
    await engine.dispose()
    print("ROUTES SMOKE TEST OK")


asyncio.run(main())
EOF

Then under `cache_lock` (`asyncio.Lock`): cache lookup via `find_reusable_scan` → `completed` hit returns 200 `cached:true`, `pending`/`running` hit returns 202 `cached:true` (in-flight dedup, same `scan_id`); on miss, `capacity_limiter.try_acquire()` → 503 if full, else `create_scan` (releasing the slot if insert fails) → spawns `run_scan` via `asyncio.create_task` (tracked in `_background_tasks` to prevent GC) → 202 `cached:false`.
  - `GET /scans/{id}` — 404 if unknown/expired (via `repo.get_scan`'s TTL filter), else status + results.
  - `GET /health` — liveness + Ollama reachability.
  - Process-wide singletons (`cache_lock`, `capacity_limiter`, `llm_client`) exposed via `Depends`-friendly getters for test overrides.
- `app/main.py` — FastAPI app with a minimal lifespan that calls `init_db()` (TTL cleanup loop comes in step 7).
- Small addition to `app/llm/client.py` (step 3 file): added `is_reachable()` to the `LLMClient` Protocol and `OllamaClient` (calls `ollama.list()`), used by `/health`.

**Verified** (temp DB, mocked LLM via dependency overrides):
- 422 for non-`.py` and empty files; 404 for unknown scan id.
- Submit → in-flight dedup (same `scan_id`, `cached:true`) while running → poll to `completed` with correct TRUE/FALSE verdicts → resubmit identical content → `cached:true`, 200, **zero additional LLM calls**.
- Capacity=1: a request while the slot is held → 503 with "capacity" in the message; after completion, slot frees and a new request is accepted.
- `/health` reflects mocked Ollama reachability (true/false).

**Also verified with real Ollama** end-to-end through the actual app (`/health` → reachable, submit → poll → `completed` with correct verdicts on the same bad-docstring/bad-variable-name sample as before).

**Not yet done (next step):** TTL cleanup task — periodic delete of scans older than `RESULT_TTL_HOURS`, wired into `main.py`'s lifespan.

USER:
in the @app/api/routes.py why do we have 1MB file size limitation?

ASSISTANT:
I added it proactively (and should have flagged it explicitly in the step 6 summary — I didn't). Reasoning:

1. **The plan's edge-case list** explicitly calls for "huge file → 422" as one of the validation cases to handle alongside empty/non-`.py`.
2. **LLM context limits**: the whole file gets embedded into each rule's prompt. A very large file could blow past `qwen2.5-coder:7b`'s context window, causing slow/garbage/failed responses rather than a clean rejection.
3. 1MB is a generous ceiling — far beyond any realistic single Python source file (most are a few KB to tens of KB) — so it's meant purely as a sanity guard, not a real constraint.

That said, it's a number I picked unilaterally and it's currently hardcoded as a magic constant. A few options:

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - FastAPI async API with SQLAlchemy 2.0 async + aiosqlite (SQLite, WAL mode, busy_timeout, foreign_keys PRAGMAs)
   - pydantic-settings for fully parametrized configuration (.env / .env.example)
   - Ollama local LLM via official `ollama` Python package's `AsyncClient`, using `format=<json schema dict>` for structured output and `options={"temperature": 0}` for determinism
   - Async separation: POST /scans (returns immediately, spawns background `asyncio.create_task`) vs GET /scans/{id} (polls result)
   - Non-blocking capacity limiting via custom `CapacityLimiter` (int counter, `try_acquire()`/`release()`, no `await` between check/increment — provably race-free in single-threaded event loop; explicitly NOT `asyncio.Semaphore` since that's designed to wait/queue)
   - Result reuse / caching: SHA-256 content hash including `RULES_VERSION` + `OLLAMA_MODEL` + normalized code; lookup matches non-expired scans in `pending`/`running`/`completed` status (in-flight dedup); `failed` scans not reused
   - `asyncio.Lock` (`cache_lock`) serializing the cache-lookup → create-scan section; defensive partial unique SQLite index on `content_hash` for `pending`/`running` rows as backstop
   - 24h TTL: lazy expiry guard already implemented in `repo.get_scan`/`find_reusable_scan` (via `_cutoff`); periodic cleanup task still pending (Step 7)
   - Rules-as-data via YAML (`app/reviewer/rules.yaml`) with `{{CODE}}` placeholder substitution (plain string replace, not `.format()`)
   - Defensive LLM verdict parsing (`parse_verdict`): strips markdown fences, parses JSON, tolerates string "true"/"false", falls back to bare token search, raises `VerdictParseError` on total failure
   - Scanner design decision: any per-rule error (LLM failure or parse failure) marks the WHOLE scan `failed` (not per-rule error status), since `rule_results.adheres` is `bool|None` with no per-row status field
   - FastAPI dependency-injection pattern for testability: `Depends(get_llm_client)`, `Depends(get_capacity_limiter)`, `Depends(get_cache_lock)`, overridable via `app.dependency_overrides` in tests
   - httpx ASGI transport (`httpx.AsyncClient(transport=ASGITransport(app=app))`) for testing FastAPI without a running server (dev-only dependency)
   - Memory system: saved `testing-style.md` (one assert per test, meaningful/edge cases only) and `incremental-step-review.md` (finish one step, pause for review) to `/Users/idansahar/.claude/projects/-Users-idansahar-Desktop-Code-Reviewer/memory/`, indexed in `MEMORY.md`

   - **`app/llm/client.py`** (current state, edited in Steps 3 and 6):
     ```python
     from __future__ import annotations

     from typing import Protocol

     import ollama

     from app.config import settings

     class LLMClient(Protocol):
         async def complete(self, prompt: str, *, json_schema: dict | None = None) -> str:
             """Send a prompt to the model and return its raw text response."""

         async def is_reachable(self) -> bool:
             """Cheap connectivity check used by /health."""

     class OllamaClient:
         """Thin wrapper around ollama.AsyncClient; base_url and model are injected
         so config.py controls which provider/model is used."""

         def __init__(
             self,
             base_url: str | None = None,
             model: str | None = None,
             timeout_seconds: float | None = None,
         ) -> None:
             self._model = model or settings.ollama_model
             self._client = ollama.AsyncClient(
                 host=base_url or settings.ollama_base_url,
                 timeout=timeout_seconds or settings.llm_timeout_seconds,
             )

         async def complete(self, prompt: str, *, json_schema: dict | None = None) -> str:
             response = await self._client.generate(
                 model=self._model,
                 prompt=prompt,
                 format=json_schema,
                 stream=False,
                 options={"temperature": 0},  # deterministic verdicts -> consistent cache hits
             )
             return response.response

         async def is_reachable(self) -> bool:
             try:
                 await self._client.list()
                 return True
             except Exception:
                 return False
     ```

   - **`app/llm/parsing.py`** (current state, edited per user's "only care about boolean" request):
     ```python
     from __future__ import annotations

     import json
     import re

     VERDICT_SCHEMA = {
         "type": "object",
         "properties": {
             "adheres": {"type": "boolean"},
             "reason": {"type": "string"},
         },
         "required": ["adheres", "reason"],
     }

     _FENCE_RE = re.compile(r"^```[a-zA-Z]*\s*|\s*```$")
     _BOOL_TOKEN_RE = re.compile(r"\b(true|false)\b", re.IGNORECASE)

     class VerdictParseError(Exception):
         """Raised when an LLM response cannot be parsed into a verdict."""

     def parse_verdict(raw: str) -> bool:
         """Parse an LLM response into an adherence verdict, tolerating common deviations."""
         text = _FENCE_RE.sub("", raw.strip()).strip()

         try:
             data = json.loads(text)
         except json.JSONDecodeError:
             data = None

         if isinstance(data, dict) and "adheres" in data:
             adheres = data["adheres"]
             if isinstance(adheres, str):
                 return adheres.strip().lower() == "true"
             return bool(adheres)

         match = _BOOL_TOKEN_RE.search(text)
         if match:
             return match.group(1).lower() == "true"

         raise VerdictParseError(f"Could not parse verdict from response: {raw!r}")
     ```

   - **`app/api/routes.py`** — **CURRENTLY MID-EDIT, NEEDS IMMEDIATE FOLLOW-UP**. Full content as last read by the system (before my latest edit) was:
     ```python
     from __future__ import annotations

     import asyncio

     from fastapi import APIRouter, Depends, File, HTTPException, Response, UploadFile, status
     from sqlalchemy.ext.asyncio import AsyncSession

     from app.config import settings
     from app.core.capacity import CapacityLimiter
     from app.core.hashing import compute_content_hash
     from app.db import repository as repo
     from app.db.models import ScanStatus
     from app.db.session import get_session
     from app.llm.client import LLMClient, OllamaClient
     from app.reviewer.scanner import run_scan
     from app.schemas import HealthResponse, RuleResultOut, ScanResultResponse, ScanSubmitResponse

     router = APIRouter()

     MAX_FILE_SIZE_BYTES = 1_000_000  # 1 MB; generous for a single source file

     # Process-wide singletons. A single asyncio.Lock serializes the cache
     # lookup -> create-scan section (see app/db/models.py for the matching
     # defensive partial unique index).
     cache_lock = asyncio.Lock()
     capacity_limiter = CapacityLimiter(max_concurrent=settings.max_parallel_scans)
     llm_client: LLMClient = OllamaClient()
     _background_tasks: set[asyncio.Task] = set()

     def get_capacity_limiter() -> CapacityLimiter:
         return capacity_limiter

     def get_llm_client() -> LLMClient:
         return llm_client

     def get_cache_lock() -> asyncio.Lock:
         return cache_lock

     @router.post("/scans", response_model=ScanSubmitResponse)
     async def submit_scan(
         response: Response,
         file: UploadFile = File(...),
         session: AsyncSession = Depends(get_session),
         limiter: CapacityLimiter = Depends(get_capacity_limiter),
         client: LLMClient = Depends(get_llm_client),
         lock: asyncio.Lock = Depends(get_cache_lock),
     ) -> ScanSubmitResponse:
         if not file.filename or not file.filename.lower().endswith(".py"):
             raise HTTPException(status.HTTP_422_UNPROCESSABLE_ENTITY, "Only .py files are accepted")

         raw = await file.read()
         if not raw:
             raise HTTPException(status.HTTP_422_UNPROCESSABLE_ENTITY, "Uploaded file is empty")
         if len(raw) > MAX_FILE_SIZE_BYTES:
             raise HTTPException(status.HTTP_422_UNPROCESSABLE_ENTITY, "File exceeds maximum size")

         try:
             code = raw.decode("utf-8")
         except UnicodeDecodeError:
             raise HTTPException(status.HTTP_422_UNPROCESSABLE_ENTITY, "File must be valid UTF-8 text")

         if not code.strip():
             raise HTTPException(status.HTTP_422_UNPROCESSABLE_ENTITY, "Uploaded file is empty")

         content_hash = compute_content_hash(code)

         async with lock:
             existing = await repo.find_reusable_scan(session, content_hash)
             if existing is not None:
                 response.status_code = (
                     status.HTTP_200_OK
                     if existing.status == ScanStatus.COMPLETED.value
                     else status.HTTP_202_ACCEPTED
                 )
                 return ScanSubmitResponse(scan_id=existing.id, status=existing.status, cached=True)

             if not limiter.try_acquire():
                 raise HTTPException(
                     status.HTTP_503_SERVICE_UNAVAILABLE,
                     f"Scan capacity reached ({settings.max_parallel_scans} concurrent scans). "
                     "Please try again later.",
                 )

             try:
                 scan = await repo.create_scan(session, content_hash, file.filename, code)
             except Exception:
                 limiter.release()
                 raise

         task = asyncio.create_task(run_scan(scan.id, code, llm_client=client, release_slot=limiter.release))
         _background_tasks.add(task)
         task.add_done_callback(_background_tasks.discard)

         response.status_code = status.HTTP_202_ACCEPTED
         return ScanSubmitResponse(scan_id=scan.id, status=scan.status, cached=False)

     @router.get("/scans/{scan_id}", response_model=ScanResultResponse)
     async def get_scan_result(scan_id: str, session: AsyncSession = Depends(get_session)) -> ScanResultResponse:
         scan = await repo.get_scan(session, scan_id)
         if scan is None:
             raise HTTPException(status.HTTP_404_NOT_FOUND, "Scan not found")

         return ScanResultResponse(
             scan_id=scan.id,
             status=scan.status,
             created_at=scan.created_at,
             results=[
                 RuleResultOut(rule_id=r.rule_id, rule_name=r.rule_name, adheres=r.adheres)
                 for r in scan.results
             ],
         )

     @router.get("/health", response_model=HealthResponse)
     async def health(client: LLMClient = Depends(get_llm_client)) -> HealthResponse:
         return HealthResponse(status="ok", ollama_reachable=await client.is_reachable())
     ```
     **I then made ONE edit to this file**: removed the line `MAX_FILE_SIZE_BYTES = 1_000_000  # 1 MB; generous for a single source file` and the blank line after it, changing:
     ```python
     router = APIRouter()

     MAX_FILE_SIZE_BYTES = 1_000_000  # 1 MB; generous for a single source file

     # Process-wide singletons.
     ```
     to:
     ```python
     router = APIRouter()
     ```

import asyncio
import datetime as dt

from app.db.session import async_session_factory, init_db

from app.db.models import Scan, ScanStatus, utcnow

async def main():
    await init_db()
    async with async_session_factory() as session:
        old = Scan(
            content_hash='old',
            filename='old.py',
            code='x=1',
            status=ScanStatus.COMPLETED.value,
        )
        old.created_at = utcnow() - dt.timedelta(hours=25)
        fresh = Scan(content_hash='fresh', filename='fresh.py', code='x=1', status=ScanStatus.COMPLETED.value)
        session.add_all([old, fresh])
        await session.commit()
        await session.refresh(old)
        await session.refresh(fresh)

        print('deleted count (expect 1):', deleted)

        print('fresh still present after cleanup (expect Scan):', (await get_scan(session, fresh.id)).id)

asyncio.run(main())

USER:
couple of questions
1) what is the lazy 404?
2) why arent we add a check in the get method (from the DB) that checks the difference between the current time and the insertion time? so if i am getting a get req but the cleanup method is between calls (between the 10 min interval)

ASSISTANT:
**1) "Lazy 404"**

It means the 404 check happens *at read time* via a query filter, rather than relying on a row having been physically deleted first. `repo.get_scan` (`app/db/repository.py:80-87`) does:

```python
.where(Scan.id == scan_id, Scan.created_at >= _cutoff(ttl_hours))
```

If `created_at` is older than `now - RESULT_TTL_HOURS`, the query simply doesn't match the row — `get_scan` returns `None` even though the row is still sitting in the table — and the route turns that into a 404. "Lazy" = expiration is enforced on-demand per request, not by a background sweep.

**2) That check already exists — it's exactly what you're describing**

The periodic cleanup task (every 10 min) only handles *physical deletion* to keep the table from growing forever. It is **not** what makes expired scans return 404.

The age check you're asking about — "compare now vs. `created_at` on every GET" — is `_cutoff()` + the `created_at >= _cutoff(...)` filter in `get_scan`, and it runs on **every single GET**, independent of the cleanup task's schedule. So if a scan turns 24h+ old at minute 3 of the 10-minute cleanup interval, a GET at minute 4 already returns 404 — the row just hasn't been deleted from disk yet.

I verified this exact scenario in the Step 7 check: a 25h-old row returned `None` from `get_scan` *before* `delete_expired_scans` was ever called, and the periodic task only later removed it from the table.

So: cleanup task = disk hygiene (bounded table size), `get_scan`'s cutoff filter = correctness guarantee (no stale results ever served). Both are needed, but they serve different purposes — and the one you're worried about (the gap between cleanup runs) is already covered by the latter.

ASSISTANT:
`CLEANUP_INTERVAL_SECONDS` is now `settings.cleanup_interval_seconds` (default 600), set in `.env`/`.env.example` alongside the other tunables, with `app/main.py` reading it from `settings`. Verified the app still starts/stops cleanly.

================================================================================
USER:
so what is the differnce between env and config files?

ASSISTANT:
In this project:

- **`.env`** — plain key/value data file with the *actual values* for your local setup (e.g. `CLEANUP_INTERVAL_SECONDS=600`). It's gitignored — every developer/deployment has their own.
- **`.env.example`** — committed template/documentation showing which variables exist and sane defaults, so someone cloning the repo knows what to copy into their own `.env`.
- **`app/config.py`** — Python code defining the `Settings` schema (pydantic-settings). It declares each setting's name, type, and default, and is configured (`env_file=".env"`) to load values from `.env` at startup, validating/coercing types (e.g. `cleanup_interval_seconds: int`). It produces the single `settings` object that the rest of the app imports.

So: `.env` = data, `config.py` = schema + loader. The app code never reads `.env` directly or uses `os.environ` — it imports `settings` from `config.py`, which is the one place that knows how to find and validate config. Note pydantic-settings' precedence: a real OS environment variable would override the same key in `.env` (useful for e.g. overriding `DATABASE_URL` in a container without editing files).

================================================================================
USER:
so the data in the config file is a default values if there is no env file?

ASSISTANT:
Exactly right.

`app/config.py` declares **fallback defaults** for every setting (e.g. `cleanup_interval_seconds: int = 600`). Pydantic-settings' lookup order is:

1. Real OS environment variable (if set)
2. Value from `.env` (if present)
3. Default from `config.py` (if neither of the above set it)

So if `.env` didn't exist at all, the app would still run using the hardcoded defaults in `config.py`. `.env` just lets you override those defaults per-environment without touching code — which is also why `extra="ignore"` is set: if `.env` has a stray key not declared in `Settings`, it's silently ignored rather than erroring.

================================================================================

  [TOOL RESULT]
1	from __future__ import annotations
2	
3	
4	class CapacityLimiter:
5	    """Non-blocking concurrency cap.
6	
7	    try_acquire() either reserves a slot and returns True, or returns False
8	    immediately if at capacity. Callers must reject the request on False, not
9	    wait for a slot to free up. Safe in a single-threaded asyncio event loop:
10	    there is no `await` between the capacity check and the increment.
11	    """
12	
13	    def __init__(self, max_concurrent: int) -> None:
14	        if max_concurrent < 1:
15	            raise ValueError("max_concurrent must be at least 1")
16	        self._max_concurrent = max_concurrent
17	        self._in_use = 0
18	
19	    def try_acquire(self) -> bool:
20	        if self._in_use >= self._max_concurrent:
21	            return False
22	        self._in_use += 1
23	        return True
24	
25	    def release(self) -> None:
26	        if self._in_use <= 0:
27	            raise RuntimeError("release() called without a matching try_acquire()")
28	        self._in_use -= 1
29	
30	    @property
31	    def in_use(self) -> int:
32	        return self._in_use
33

1	from __future__ import annotations
2	
3	import hashlib
4	
5	from app.config import settings
6	
7	
8	def compute_content_hash(code: str) -> str:
9	    """Hash of the code plus the rules version and model that will check it.
10	
11	    Including RULES_VERSION and OLLAMA_MODEL means a cached verdict is only
12	    reused if it was produced by the same rules and the same model.
13	    """
14	    normalized = code.replace("\r\n", "\n").strip()
15	    payload = f"{settings.rules_version}\0{settings.ollama_model}\0{normalized}"
16	    return hashlib.sha256(payload.encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()

1	from __future__ import annotations
2	
3	import json
4	import re
5	
6	VERDICT_SCHEMA = {
7	    "type": "object",
8	    "properties": {
9	        "adheres": {"type": "boolean"},
10	        "reason": {"type": "string"},
11	    },
12	    "required": ["adheres", "reason"],
13	}
14	
15	_FENCE_RE = re.compile(r"^```[a-zA-Z]*\s*|\s*```$")
16	_BOOL_TOKEN_RE = re.compile(r"\b(true|false)\b", re.IGNORECASE)
17	
18	
19	class VerdictParseError(Exception):
20	    """Raised when an LLM response cannot be parsed into a verdict."""
21	
22	
23	def parse_verdict(raw: str) -> bool:
24	    """Parse an LLM response into an adherence verdict, tolerating common deviations."""
25	    text = _FENCE_RE.sub("", raw.strip()).strip()
26	
27	    try:
28	        data = json.loads(text)
29	    except json.JSONDecodeError:
30	        data = None
31	
32	    if isinstance(data, dict) and "adheres" in data:
33	        adheres = data["adheres"]
34	        if isinstance(adheres, str):
35	            return adheres.strip().lower() == "true"
36	        return bool(adheres)
37	
38	    match = _BOOL_TOKEN_RE.search(text)
39	    if match:
40	        return match.group(1).lower() == "true"
41	
42	    raise VerdictParseError

- **`tests/helpers.py`** — `MockLLMClient` (records prompts, scripted verdicts/exceptions/raw responses, optional blocking via `asyncio.Event`), `code_for`/`make_py_file`, `wait_for_new_tasks`.

- **`pytest.ini`** — `asyncio_mode = auto` + session-scoped event loop (required so the SQLAlchemy async engine/connection pool isn't shared across mismatched loops).
- **`tests/test_api.py`** (5)** — full submit→poll→results flow with per-rule verdicts; non-`.py` upload 422; empty file 422; unknown id 404; unparseable LLM response → scan `failed`.
- **`tests/test_capacity.py`** (4) — 503 when at capacity; slot freed after completion (next request succeeds); LLM exception → scan `failed`; LLM exception → capacity slot still released.
- **`tests/test_cache.py`** (4) — identical content → zero new LLM calls; changing `OLLAMA_MODEL` → cache miss (new scan); two truly-concurrent identical POSTs → exactly one DB row; failed scan not reused (new scan on resubmit).
- **`tests/test_ttl.py`** (2) — 25h-old row → `get_scan` returns `None` before cleanup (lazy expiry); `delete_expired_scans` physically removes it.
- **`tests/test_parsing.py`** (6) — `parse_verdict` edge cases: JSON true/false, markdown-fenced JSON, string `"true"`, bare-token fallback, garbage → `VerdictParseError`.

1	We want to build an automatic Code Review Platform!
2	We'll start with a simple POC, that will show the full E2E flow - requesting a scan, analyzing the code, and fetching the results.
3	
4	The system is comprised of 2 parts:
5	      • The Code-Reviewer: given a source code file (python), it runs a set of pre-defined singular checks (each defined using a prompt) against the code and identifies to which rules the code adheres to and to which it doesn't.
6	      • The Platform: gets a scan request from the user (containing the code file) via API, scans it (using the Code-Reviewer), and makes its output accessible for fetching via a dedicated API. 
7	
8	Rules to be checked:
9	      1) All variables have meaningful names
10	      2)  docstring of function reflects the actual code’s logic
11	
12	Requirements:
13	      1) Rules might be added overtime and total analysis time might exceed connection limitations, therefore scan requesting and results fetching must be separated (asynchronous).
14	      2) Scan results should show users the list of all checked rules, and for each whether it is adhered to or not (TRUE/FALSE)
15	      3) System should support up to 5 parallel scans. For POC,

```bash

```
Then inside the prompt:
```sql
.tables

SELECT id, status, filename, created_at FROM scans ORDER BY created_at DESC;
SELECT * FROM rule_results WHERE scan_id = '<scan_id>';
```
`.headers on` and `.mode column` make output readable.

USER:
and if i want to clean the DB how do i do it?

ASSISTANT:
Two options, depending on whether you want a full reset or just to empty the tables:

**1. Full reset (delete the DB files)** — simplest. Make sure the server isn't running, then:
```bash
rm -f code_review.db code_review.db-wal code_review.db-shm code_review.db-journal
```
Next time you start `uvicorn`, `init_db()` recreates empty tables automatically (this is what we did for test DBs).

**2. Empty the tables but keep the file** — works while the server is running, via `sqlite3`:
```bash
sqlite3 code_review.db "PRAGMA foreign_keys=ON; DELETE FROM scans;"
```
The `ON DELETE CASCADE` foreign key (with `PRAGMA foreign_keys=ON`) takes care of `rule_results` automatically.

For your current 9 rows from the E2E run, option 1 is probably cleanest. Want me to run it?

================================================================================
USER:
not right now, can i use the FastAPI web gui for upload scans?

ASSISTANT:
Yes — FastAPI auto-generates an interactive Swagger UI at **`/docs`** (and a read-only ReDoc at `/redoc`), no extra setup needed.

1. Start the server: `uvicorn app.main:app --reload`
2. Open `http://localhost:8000/docs`
3. Expand **`POST /scans`** → click **"Try it out"** → it shows a file picker for the `file` field (since it's `multipart/form-data`) → choose a `.py` file → **"Execute"**
4. The response panel shows the JSON (`scan_id`, `status`, `cached`)
5. Expand **`GET /scans/{scan_id}`** → "Try it out" → paste the `scan_id` → "Execute" to poll for results

Only `/docs` (Swagger) supports "Try it out"; `/redoc` is documentation-only.

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - FastAPI async API with SQLAlchemy 2.0 async + aiosqlite (SQLite, WAL mode, busy_timeout=5000, foreign_keys PRAGMA)
   - pydantic-settings (`app/config.py`) — single source of truth `settings` object, env var > `.env` > field default precedence, `extra="ignore"`
   - Ollama local LLM via official `ollama` Python package's `AsyncClient`, `format=<json schema>`, `options={"temperature": 0}`, `timeout=settings.llm_timeout_seconds` passed to underlying httpx client
   - Async separation: `POST /scans` (202, spawns `asyncio.create_task`) vs `GET /scans/{id}` (polls)
   - `CapacityLimiter` (custom int-counter class in `app/core/capacity.py`, NOT `asyncio.Semaphore`) — `try_acquire()`/`release()`, race-free in single-threaded event loop
   - Result reuse / caching via `compute_content_hash` (SHA-256 of `RULES_VERSION + OLLAMA_MODEL + normalized code`); `cache_lock` (`asyncio.Lock`) serializes cache-lookup→create-scan
   - 24h TTL: lazy expiry via `_cutoff()` filter in `repo.get_scan`/`find_reusable_scan` (immediate, query-time) PLUS periodic `_cleanup_loop()` background task (physical deletion, every `CLEANUP_INTERVAL_SECONDS`)
   - Rules-as-data via YAML (`app/reviewer/rules.yaml`) with shared `PROMPT_TEMPLATE` containing `{{RULE}}` and `{{CODE}}` placeholders, substituted in `Rule.build_prompt()`
   - Defensive LLM verdict parsing (`parse_verdict` in `app/llm/parsing.py`) — returns bool only, tolerates markdown fences, string booleans, bare-token fallback, raises `VerdictParseError`
   - FastAPI dependency-injection pattern: `Depends(get_llm_client)`, `Depends(get_capacity_limiter)`, `Depends(get_cache_lock)`, overridable via `app.dependency_overrides`
   - pytest-asyncio 1.4.0 session-scoped event loop (`asyncio_default_fixture_loop_scope`/`asyncio_default_test_loop_scope = session`) — required to avoid SQLAlchemy async engine cross-loop errors
   - httpx `ASGITransport` for testing FastAPI without a running server
   - Ollama's default `keep_alive` behavior — models get unloaded from memory after idle period (relevant to current investigation: `ollama ps` shows empty, suggesting `qwen2.5-coder:7b` (4.7GB) was evicted and needs reloading from disk, which is slow)
   - macOS `zsh`: `status` is a read-only shell variable (caused an error, fixed by renaming to `scan_status`)

     ```
     OLLAMA_BASE_URL=http://localhost:11434

     # Seconds to wait for a single LLM call before treating it as failed
     LLM_TIMEOUT_SECONDS=120

     # Max number of scans running concurrently; further requests get 503
     MAX_PARALLEL_SCANS=5

     # How long scan results are kept before being deleted
     RESULT_TTL_HOURS=24

     # How often the background task sweeps expired scans (seconds)
     CLEANUP_INTERVAL_SECONDS=600

     DATABASE_URL=sqlite+aiosqlite:///./code_review.db

     # Bump this when rule prompts change to invalidate previously cached verdicts
     RULES_VERSION=v1

     # Reject uploads larger than this (bytes)
     MAX_FILE_SIZE_BYTES=1000000
     ```

   - **`app/main.py`** (current full state):
     ```python
     from __future__ import annotations

     import asyncio
     import contextlib
     from collections.abc import AsyncIterator

     from fastapi import FastAPI

     from app.api.routes import router
     from app.config import settings
     from app.db.repository import delete_expired_scans
     from app.db.session import async_session_factory, init_db

     async def _cleanup_loop() -> None:
         while True:
             await asyncio.sleep(settings.cleanup_interval_seconds)
             async with async_session_factory() as session:
                 await delete_expired_scans(session)

     @contextlib.asynccontextmanager
     async def lifespan(app: FastAPI) -> AsyncIterator[None]:
         await init_db()
         task = asyncio.create_task(_cleanup_loop())
         try:
             yield
         finally:
             task.cancel()
             with contextlib.suppress(asyncio.CancelledError):
                 await task

     app = FastAPI(title="Code Review Platform", lifespan=lifespan)
     app.include_router(router)
     ```

     ```yaml
     rules:
       - id: meaningful_variable_names
         name: All variables have meaningful names
         rule: |
           All variables (including function parameters, loop variables, and
           attributes) must have meaningful, descriptive names. Single-letter names,
           generic names like `x`, `tmp`, `data`, `val`, `foo`, or unclear abbreviations
           violate this rule. Short-lived loop counters such as `i`/`j` in simple loops,
           and conventional names like `self`/`cls`, are acceptable.

       - id: docstring_matches_logic
         name: Docstring of function reflects the actual code's logic
         rule: |
           For every function or method that has a docstring, the docstring must
           accurately describe what the code actually does (parameters, return value,
           and behavior). A function with no docstring does not violate this rule -
           only an existing docstring that contradicts or misrepresents the
           implementation is a violation.
     ```

ASSISTANT:
Found it. Here's the chain of events, reconstructed from `~/.ollama/logs/server.log` and the DB:

**1. The model had been unloaded since Step 10**
Step 10's last LLM call was at 11:24:56 (local time). Ollama's default `keep_alive` unloads idle models after ~5 min, so by the time you uploaded `mixed_violations.py` at 11:36:47, `qwen2.5-coder:7b` (4.7GB) was no longer in memory — `ollama ps` is empty right now too.

**2. The reload-on-demand failed**
The log shows Ollama starting to reload the model from disk for this request, finishing in 3.47s, then:
```
[GIN] 11:36:53 | 500 | 6.048s | POST "/api/generate"
```
Ollama returned an **HTTP 500** after 6 seconds — not a timeout, an actual server error. This lines up exactly with your scan's `created_at` (08:36:47 UTC = 11:36:47 local). Almost certainly Ollama failed to reload the model because the system was under severe memory pressure at that moment (`top` showed 17G/17G used, only 72MB free) — a known Ollama failure mode is "model requires more system memory than is available."

**3. But here's the actual bug: the scan never transitioned to `failed`**
`run_scan()` has a `try/except Exception` that's supposed to catch exactly this (`ollama.ResponseError` from the 500), call `mark_failed`, and release the capacity slot. Instead, 6 minutes later, the DB row is still:
```
status=running, completed_at=NULL, error=NULL, rule_results=(none)
```
So something inside that `except` block (most likely `mark_failed`'s own `session.commit()`, possibly a transient SQLite lock) threw a *second* exception that escaped uncaught — since the scan task is fire-and-forget (`asyncio.create_task`), nothing surfaces that error except a traceback printed to **your uvicorn terminal** (the one running `--reload`). I can't see that terminal — could you scroll back in it and check for a traceback around 11:36:53? That'll tell us exactly what failed in the except path.

**Practical side-effect**: this scan is now permanently stuck at `running` (until the 24h TTL sweep deletes it). Worse — `find_reusable_scan` treats `running` as cacheable, so if you resubmit `mixed_violations.py` right now, you'll get `cached: true` pointing at this same stuck scan, which will look like it's "hanging" again.

Want to check the terminal traceback first, or should I look at hardening `run_scan`'s error handling (e.g. catch `BaseException` / wrap `mark_failed` itself in a fallback) once we know the root cause?

USER:
look at hardening the run_scan error handeling and also handle what happens if the job is getting hanged for some other reason on "running" status - making sure that the timeout will work and change it to failed (in this case the time out didnt worked)

ASSISTANT:
I'll lay out the plan and then implement it across the few files involved:

**A. Harden `run_scan` (scanner.py)**
- Wrap each per-rule LLM call in `asyncio.wait_for(timeout=settings.llm_timeout_seconds)` with a descriptive `TimeoutError` — makes the configured timeout an actual hard cutoff, independent of whatever `ollama.AsyncClient`'s own timeout does internally.
- Wrap `mark_failed` in its own try/except, so if *persisting the failure* itself errors (the bug that left this scan stuck at `running`), we log it but `finally: release_slot()` still runs.

**B. "Stale running" watchdog (safety net for crashes/unrecoverable cases)**
- New config `SCAN_STALE_SECONDS` (default 300s) in `config.py` / `.env` / `.env.example`.
- `repository.py`: `get_scan` lazily flips an old `running` row to `failed` (mirrors the existing lazy-TTL pattern) + a new `fail_stale_scans()` bulk sweep.
- `routes.py`: run `fail_stale_scans()` before the cache-reuse lookup in `POST /scans`, so resubmitting the same content doesn't latch onto a dead `running` row.
- `main.py`: call `fail_stale_scans()` from the existing periodic cleanup loop.

**C. Tests** for: LLM-call timeout → `failed`, `mark_failed` itself raising doesn't crash the task, lazy stale→failed on GET, resubmit doesn't reuse a stale running row, periodic sweep.

23	async def lifespan(app: FastAPI) -> AsyncIterator[None]:
24	    await init_db()
25	    task = asyncio.create_task(_cleanup_loop())
26	    try:
27	        yield
28	    finally:
29	        task.cancel()
30	        with contextlib.suppress(asyncio.CancelledError):
31	            await task

ASSISTANT:
Done. Summary of what changed:

**`app/reviewer/scanner.py`**
- Each per-rule LLM call is now wrapped in `asyncio.wait_for(timeout=settings.llm_timeout_seconds)`, raising a descriptive `TimeoutError` on expiry — the configured timeout is now an actual app-level cutoff, not dependent on `ollama.AsyncClient`'s internal behavior.
- `mark_failed` is now wrapped in its own try/except, so if *persisting* the failure errors too, it's logged but `finally: release_slot()` still runs (this was the actual cause of the stuck scan).

**New "stale running" watchdog** (config `SCAN_STALE_SECONDS=300`, in `.env`/`.env.example`/`config.py`):
- `repository.get_scan` lazily flips an old `running` row to `failed` (mirrors the existing lazy-TTL pattern) — confirmed live: `GET /scans/{stuck_id}` now returns `status: failed, error: "Scan timed out"`, and the DB row is persisted that way.
- `repository.fail_stale_scans()` does the same as a bulk sweep, called from the periodic `_cleanup_loop` in `main.py`.
- `routes.py` runs `fail_stale_scans()` before the cache-reuse lookup in `POST /scans`, so resubmitting identical content won't latch onto a dead `running` row.

**Tests** — added `tests/test_resilience.py` (5 new tests, one assert each): LLM timeout → `failed`; `mark_failed` itself raising still releases the slot; lazy stale→failed on GET; resubmit doesn't reuse a stale `running` row; periodic sweep marks stale rows `failed`. Full suite: **26/26 passing**.

The originally-stuck `mixed_violations.py` scan (`c47b43e7-...`) is now `failed` in the DB. You can resubmit that file via `/docs` and it'll create a fresh scan — Ollama is reachable now, though the model may still need a cold reload (worth checking system memory pressure if it's slow again, that root cause is separate from what we fixed here).

USER:
but i can see in the DB that there are 6 jobs that were completeted  - dont we need to have 5?

ASSISTANT:
That's expected — `MAX_PARALLEL_SCANS=5` limits how many scans can run **concurrently**, not how many can run in total over time.

Breakdown of the 6 completed rows:
- **5** came from the initial batch of 8 concurrent submissions (the ones that got `202` — the other 3 got `503` and were never created as scan rows at all).
- **1** (`25c4ba65...`) was the 9th submission I sent *after* those 5 finished and freed their slots — that was the final check confirming the capacity slot gets released properly once a scan completes.

So at no point were more than 5 scans running simultaneously (verified by the polling output — exactly 5 `running` at a time, then they drained down). The 6th completed row is just a 6th *sequential* scan, not a 6th concurrent one — capacity limiting is working correctly.

ASSISTANT:
I haven't changed it back — `app/api/routes.py` still uses `HTTP_422_UNPROCESSABLE_CONTENT` in all 5 places (just verified via grep).

What you're likely seeing is the **HTTP response itself** showing `422 Unprocessable Entity` — and that's expected, because:

- `HTTP_422_UNPROCESSABLE_ENTITY` and `HTTP_422_UNPROCESSABLE_CONTENT` are just **two different names for the same integer, `422`**, both still defined in `starlette.status`.
- The actual reason phrase sent on the wire comes from Python's stdlib `http.HTTPStatus(422).phrase`, which is hardcoded to `"Unprocessable Entity"` — Python hasn't adopted RFC 9110's 2022 rename to "Unprocessable Content".

So no matter which constant name we reference in our code, the response line will always read `422 Unprocessable Entity` — that's controlled by Python/uvicorn, not by which alias we pick. The rename we did earlier was purely to silence FastAPI's `DeprecationWarning` about the old constant *name* (`_ENTITY` is the deprecated identifier in `starlette.status`, scheduled for removal); it has no effect on the response itself.

Nothing to fix here — this is just how 422 looks regardless.

USER:
just to make sure, the clean up is only happening when the system is up right?

ASSISTANT:
Yes, correct — both cleanup mechanisms (the periodic loop and the lazy per-request checks) only run while the FastAPI process/event loop is alive. There's no external cron job or separate process.

Concretely:
- **Periodic sweep** (`_cleanup_loop` in `app/main.py`): an `asyncio.create_task` started in `lifespan`. If the server is down, this task doesn't exist — nothing runs.
- **Lazy checks** (TTL expiry on `GET`, and the new stale-running fixups on `GET`/`POST`): only execute as part of handling an actual HTTP request.

Practical implication: if the server is down for a while, expired/stale rows just sit in the DB untouched. As soon as it restarts, the lazy checks immediately make expired/stale rows behave correctly (404, or `failed`) the next time they're accessed — but *physical deletion* of expired rows waits for the periodic loop's first tick (up to `CLEANUP_INTERVAL_SECONDS` after startup).

**1. App startup triggers it** — `app/main.py:24`
```python
async def lifespan(app: FastAPI) -> AsyncIterator[None]:
    await init_db()
```
This runs once when uvicorn starts the app (FastAPI's `lifespan` context manager).

**2. `init_db()` creates the tables** — `app/db/session.py:26-28`
```python
async def init_db() -> None:
    async with engine.begin() as conn:
        await conn.run_sync(Base.metadata.create_all)
```
`Base.metadata.create_all` issues `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` (+ indexes) for every table registered on `Base`. It's idempotent — safe to call on every startup, only creates what's missing.

**3. The engine / DB file** — `app/db/session.py:11`
```python
engine = create_async_engine(settings.database_url)
```
`settings.database_url` comes from `.env`: `sqlite+aiosqlite:///./code_review.db`. The first time the engine actually connects (inside `init_db()`'s `engine.begin()`), `aiosqlite`/SQLite creates `code_review.db` on disk if it doesn't exist — there's no separate "create the file" step.

**4. Every connection gets the same PRAGMAs** — `app/db/session.py:14-20`
```python
@event.listens_for(engine.sync_engine, "connect")
def _set_sqlite_pragmas(dbapi_connection, _connection_record) -> None:
    cursor.execute("PRAGMA journal_mode=WAL")
    cursor.execute("PRAGMA busy_timeout=5000")
    cursor.execute("PRAGMA foreign_keys=ON")
```
This fires on *every* new connection from the pool, not just the first.

**5. The tables themselves are defined in `app/db/models.py`** — both inherit from `Base(DeclarativeBase)` (`models.py:11-12`), which is what `Base.metadata` in step 2 walks:

- **`Scan`** (`models.py:26-52`) → table `scans`: `id`, `content_hash`, `filename`, `code`, `status`, `created_at`, `completed_at`, `error`, plus `__table_args__` with two regular indexes and a partial unique index (`content_hash` unique only among `pending`/`running` rows — the in-flight-dedup backstop).
- **`RuleResult`** (`models.py:55-65`) → table `rule_results`: `id`, `scan_id` (FK → `scans.id`, `ON DELETE CASCADE`), `rule_id`, `rule_name`, `adheres`, `detail`. The `relationship(..., cascade="all, delete-orphan")` on `Scan.results` means deleting a scan row deletes its rule results too.

**6. Everything else reuses the same engine** — `async_session_factory` (`session.py:23`) is the sessionmaker built on top of `engine`; it's what `get_session` (the FastAPI dependency), `scanner._run`, and `_cleanup_loop` all use to open sessions against this same SQLite file.

So: one `Settings.database_url` → one `engine` → `init_db()` (called once at startup) creates `scans` + `rule_results` (and indexes) from the `Base`-registered model classes in `models.py`.

USER:
explain to me about the async_session_factory

ASSISTANT:
`async_session_factory` is the thing every part of the app calls when it needs a database session. Defined in `app/db/session.py:23`:

```python
async_session_factory = async_sessionmaker(engine, expire_on_commit=False)
```

**What it is**

`async_sessionmaker(engine, ...)` doesn't create a session itself — it returns a *callable* that, when invoked (`async_session_factory()`), produces a new `AsyncSession` bound to `engine`. Think of it as a pre-configured "session constructor."

**Why a factory instead of one shared session**

An `AsyncSession` represents a single unit of work / transaction and is **not safe to share** across concurrent requests or tasks. Every request, and every background task iteration, needs its *own* session. The factory lets any part of the code cheaply spin up a fresh one, all backed by the same connection pool (`engine`).

**`expire_on_commit=False` — the important bit**

By default, SQLAlchemy expires all loaded objects after `session.commit()` — the next attribute access triggers a fresh `SELECT` to reload it ("lazy refresh"). For **async** SQLAlchemy, that implicit lazy-load is a problem: it requires I/O, and accessing an attribute outside an `await`ed context raises `MissingGreenlet`. `expire_on_commit=False` disables that expiry, so objects keep their already-loaded values after commit and can be safely read afterward (e.g. `repo.create_scan` does `commit()` + `refresh()`, then `routes.py` reads `scan.id`/`scan.status` on the result — that only works because attributes aren't expired).

**Where it's actually used**

1. **Per-request, via DI** — `get_session()` (`session.py:31-33`):
   ```python
   async def get_session() -> AsyncGenerator[AsyncSession, None]:
       async with async_session_factory() as session:
           yield session
   ```
   FastAPI calls this once per request (`Depends(get_session)`); the session lives for the request's duration and closes when the generator resumes after the response.

2. **Per repo-call, in background scans** — `scanner.py`'s `_run` helper:
   ```python
   async def _run(fn, *args):
       async with async_session_factory() as session:
           return await fn(session, *args)
   ```
   `run_scan` runs as a detached `asyncio.create_task`, completely outside any request's session lifecycle — so each step (`mark_running`, `save_rule_result`, `mark_completed`/`mark_failed`) opens its own short-lived session/transaction via `_run`.

3. **In the cleanup loop** — `main.py`'s `_cleanup_loop` opens one session per tick to run `fail_stale_scans` + `delete_expired_scans`.

**The `async with ... as session:` pattern**: on exit, the session is closed and its connection returned to the engine's pool — whether the block succeeds or raises. Note it doesn't auto-commit; each repo function calls `session.commit()` explicitly when it wants its writes persisted.

USER:
explain to me what is a session, it is like another connection to the DB for each tread?

ASSISTANT:
Not quite — a session isn't itself a connection, and it's not "per thread" here (this app is single-threaded/async). Let me untangle the layers.

**The layers, bottom to top:**

1. **Connection** — an actual physical link to the DB (for SQLite via `aiosqlite`, basically a `sqlite3` connection/file handle). Opening one has real cost.

2. **Engine + connection pool** — `engine = create_async_engine(...)` (one per app, created once). It maintains a **pool** of these physical connections, handing them out on demand and taking them back when done, so you're not constantly opening/closing files.

3. **Session** — a higher-level object that represents *one unit of work*. It is **not** a connection itself — it's more like a workspace that:
   - **borrows** a connection from the engine's pool, but only when it actually needs to talk to the DB (first query/flush), not at creation time
   - tracks an **identity map**: "this Python `Scan` object = row with id X" — so if you fetch the same row twice in one session, you get the same object back
   - tracks pending changes (adds/updates/deletes) and writes them on `commit()`/`flush()`
   - **returns the connection to the pool** when the transaction ends (commit/rollback) or the session closes

So: many sessions can exist, but they share the same small pool of underlying connections, borrowing/returning as needed.

**About "per thread"**

The pattern you're thinking of is real for *synchronous* SQLAlchemy apps — e.g. Flask's `scoped_session`, where each request thread transparently gets its own session via thread-local storage, because sharing one Session across threads would corrupt its identity map / in-flight transaction.

This app is single-threaded async, so the equivalent unit isn't "thread" — it's **"logical unit of work."** There's no automatic thread-local magic; instead, the code *explicitly* calls `async_session_factory()` every time it starts a new unit of work:

- **Per HTTP request**: `get_session()` creates one session, used for the whole request.
- **Per scan-lifecycle step**: in `scanner.py`, `_run()` opens a *brand new* session for *each* call — `mark_running`, then later `save_rule_result` (×2), then `mark_completed`/`mark_failed` are **4 separate sessions/transactions**, not one long-lived session for the whole scan. This makes sense because `run_scan` is a detached background task that spans seconds/minutes — holding one open transaction that whole time would be wasteful and could block other writers.
- **Per cleanup tick**: `_cleanup_loop` opens one session, does its sweeps, closes it.

The reason it's "one session per X" rather than sharing is the same reason as the threaded case: a `Session`'s identity map and pending-changes state aren't safe to use from two concurrent contexts at once — whether those contexts are threads (sync world) or coroutines/tasks (this app's world).

USER:
so its basicly given at any time a chagne (read/wrtie) neds to be done on the Db? and also what do you mean by commit/flush?

ASSISTANT:
**On #1 — yes, roughly:**

A session is the required "handle" for *any* ORM interaction with the DB — read or write. You can't run a query or persist an object without one. So the pattern is: whenever a piece of code needs to talk to the DB at all, it does so inside a session (`async with async_session_factory() as session: ...`).

Within that session, you can do multiple reads and writes — e.g. `mark_completed` does a **read** (`session.get(Scan, scan_id)`) followed by a **write** (mutating `scan.status`, then `commit()`) — all in the same session/transaction.

**On #2 — flush vs. commit:**

Both relate to "when do my Python-side changes actually get sent to the database, and when do they become permanent."

- **`flush()`** — sends the pending SQL (INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE) to the database, *as part of the current transaction*, but doesn't finalize it. Other connections/sessions still can't see it, and if something goes wrong before commit, it can be rolled back as if it never happened.
  - This happens **automatically** before most queries (SQLAlchemy's "autoflush") — so if you `session.add(new_obj)` and then run a `SELECT`, your pending insert is flushed first so the query sees consistent state.
  - Flush is also when DB-generated values get populated back onto your object (e.g. an autoincrement `id`).

- **`commit()`** — flushes (if needed) **and then** tells the database to make the transaction permanent (`COMMIT`). After this, the changes are durable and visible to other connections. The session then implicitly starts a fresh transaction for whatever comes next.

**Concrete example**, `repo.create_scan`:
```python
scan = Scan(content_hash=..., filename=..., code=..., status="pending")
session.add(scan)        # staged in memory — nothing sent yet
await session.commit()   # flush (INSERT sent) + commit (made permanent)
await session.refresh(scan)  # re-read row from DB
return scan
```

Until `commit()`, `scan` exists only as a pending object inside that session — nothing is in `code_review.db` yet, and another session/process querying the table wouldn't see it. After `commit()`, it's a real row.

Why this matters for the "one session per step" pattern in `scanner.py`: each `_run(repo.mark_running, ...)`, `_run(repo.save_rule_result, ...)`, etc. opens its own session and commits before closing — so each step's write is durable and visible to anyone (e.g. a `GET /scans/{id}` from another request) immediately, rather than only becoming visible at the very end of the whole scan.
